Chiang Kai-shek Returns to Nanchang 102

Summons Gu Xiong and Others, Directs Suppression Strategies

Nanchang Dispatch: Chairman Chiang Kai-shek, having completed his tour of the Northwest, inspecting Hubei, Henan, Shaanxi, Gansu, Ningxia, Shandong, Hebei, Chahar, Suiyuan, Shanxi, Beiping, Hankou, and other provinces and cities, returned to Nanchang by Eurasia Airlines' large aircraft at 12:00 noon on the 12th from Jiujiang. Details are as follows:

Chairman Chiang Kai-shek left the province in June and was stationed at Guling, presiding over the second phase of military training at Haihui Temple. Trainees included over 8,000 middle and senior-level military officers from Hebei, Shandong, Chahar, Suiyuan, Shaanxi, Gansu, Henan, Hubei, Anhui, Jiangxi, Hunan, Fujian, Guangdong, and Guangxi provinces. After the summer military training concluded, he departed Guling on October 4th, traveling westward via Hankou. He inspected Luoyang, Xi'an, Lanzhou, Ningxia, Kaifeng, Zhengzhou, Jinan, Beiping, Zhangjiakou, Suiyuan, Taiyuan, and Datong, among other places. He met with military and political leaders everywhere, providing instructions. Especially in the border areas of Suiyuan, Chahar, Ningxia, and Gansu, Chairman Chiang Kai-shek's deep entry into the desolate regions, comforting the suffering people, was exceptionally inspiring. It holds profound significance for uniting the Mongol and Hui people, consolidating border defenses, developing the Northwest, and reviving the inherent culture of the nation. Chairman Chiang Kai-shek also gained a very positive impression of the various regions during this trip. Due to the importance of suppressing bandits, he returned south from Taiyuan by Eurasia Airlines' large aircraft at 12:00 noon on the 11th. He arrived in Hankou at 3:00 PM. Originally, he planned to continue to Jiangxi on the same aircraft, but due to unfavorable weather conditions, he traveled eastward from Hankou on the Yong Sui warship at 8:00 PM on the 11th. He arrived in Xunyang at 9:15 AM on the 12th. Chinese and foreign warships fired salutes, and the whole city hung flags in enthusiastic welcome. Chen Lei, the 9th Garrison Commander, Li Zhongxiang, the Director of the Municipal Council, and Bao Gongren, the County Magistrate, all stood respectfully at the dock to greet him. After Chairman Chiang Kai-shek disembarked and greeted the welcoming crowd, he proceeded directly to the airfield and boarded the Eurasia Airlines' large aircraft that had been flown in from Hankou and was waiting for him. He flew to the province around 10:00 AM. After receiving a phone call from Jiujiang, the Nanchang Aviation Station immediately reported to the headquarters and the provincial government. After the Sun Yat-sen birthday memorial week was dismissed, military and political leaders rushed to the airfield outside the city to greet him. Those present included Ding Chaowu, Tai Shih-hui, Gu Zhutong, He Guoguang, Chen Qingyun, Wang Yitang, and over 200 other senior officials from the provincial capital. At 11:30 AM, the large aircraft arrived from the north with a rumbling sound, circling the city once before landing at the airfield amidst uplifting military music. All welcoming personnel went to the aircraft to salute and welcome him. Chairman Chiang Kai-shek, wearing a blue robe and a black mandarin jacket, draped with a black cloak, slowly disembarked and repeatedly nodded to those welcoming him, expressing his gratitude. He shook hands with Wang Yitang, exchanging greetings. He then boarded a headquarters car and went directly to his private residence in Beitan. Accompanying Chairman Chiang Kai-shek were Secretary Li Rizhang and several bodyguards. Madame Chiang had already gone to Beiping. Yang Yongtai and his staff were traveling south via the Beiping-Hankou Railway and are expected to arrive tomorrow. Li Jingcong, the manager of Eurasia Airlines, accompanied Chairman Chiang Kai-shek on the same aircraft, taking care of everything along the way.

After arriving at his private residence, Chairman Chiang Kai-shek met with Tai Shih-hui, Gu Zhutong, He Guoguang, and others, listening to reports on the bandit suppression military affairs in the province, the aftermath in the recovered areas, and all matters pertaining to the headquarters. Chairman Chiang Kai-shek gave instructions on everything. He also had meticulous plans for intercepting Zhu De and Mao Zedong, and annihilating the bandit leaders Xu Xiangqian, He Long, and Xiao Ke. (November 12th)

Expansion of the Beiping City Area 103

Beiping to Become a Purely Cultural City

Area Boundaries to Be Redefined

Beiping Dispatch: Due to Beiping's history as a capital for hundreds of years, its cultural relics, historical heritage, and cultural artifacts hold the most superior position in the country. Therefore, after the September 18th Incident, intellectuals and social figures suggested turning Beiping into a cultural city, permanently without troops stationed or military institutions established. It is reported that a certain magnate recently arrived in Beiping, and Mayor Yuan Liang presented a proposal to expand the Beiping area, introduce rivers, and incorporate scenic spots such as the Big and Small Tangshan Mountains and the Eight Great Sites of Fragrant Hills in western Beijing, to transform Beiping into a purely beautified city. The magnate also believes that, in terms of political and diplomatic relations, it is necessary to simultaneously upgrade Beiping and Tianjin into special municipalities. Thus, the expansion of the Beiping area is being resolutely carried out. Recently, it was heard that the municipal authorities have drafted various designs for the new metropolitan area, assigning famous scholars and Beijing historical and geographical experts to various positions. Minister of Finance Kong Xiangxi also came to Beiping with financial specialists to make provisions for the future division of financial areas and the establishment of tax collection agencies. Military and government offices may also have to be slightly relocated for ease of control. The general scope of the city expansion is as follows: 1. Area: The southern suburbs of Daxing and Wanping counties (the offices of these two counties were originally located within the city of Beijing, one administering the eastern city and the other administering the western city; after the Northern Expedition of the Kuomintang, one was moved to Lugou Bridge), including Nanyuan, Huangcun, Fengtai, Caiyu Town, Lixian Town, Qingyundian, Sunhe Town (all belonging to Daxing), Changxindian, Langouqiao, Mentougou, Qinghe Town, as well as the Big and Small Tangshan Mountains in northern Beiping and the Fragrant Hills, Longevity Mountain, and Eight Great Sites in western Beiping, are all incorporated into the city. The endpoint of the entire city extends east to Tongzhou, north to Changping, west to Liangxiang, and south to Anci. The Ming Tombs are also included within the city's boundaries. 2. Boundaries: The eastern suburbs from Dongba and Bailu Temple to the western suburbs of Sanjiadian, the southern boundary is Dahuangmen, and the northern boundary is Yangfang, spanning 76 li from east to west and 60 li from north to south, covering an area of approximately 1,750 square li. The inner city is 10 li wide and long, covering an area of 100 square li. The Imperial City is 18 li in circumference, occupying about one-fifth of the inner city. The Forbidden City is 6 li in circumference, occupying one-quarter of the Imperial City. The Three Seas occupy two-ninths of the Imperial City. The outer city is 28 li in circumference, covering an area of 96 li. 3. Historical Names and Evolution: Beiping was originally named Beijing. In historical records, it is the old Jizhou area of Yu's Nine Provinces. During the Zhou Dynasty, the descendants of Yao were enfeoffed in Ji, and the descendants of Duke Zhao were enfeoffed in Yan. During the Later Wei and Qi Zhou dynasties, it was called Yan Commandery. During the Tang Dynasty, it was called Youzhou. During the Song Dynasty, it was called Yanshan Prefecture. During the Liao Dynasty, it was elevated to the status of Nanjing. During the Yuan Dynasty, it was rebuilt as Dadu. During the Ming Dynasty, it was renamed Beiping Prefecture and designated as the fiefdom of the Prince of Yan. In the first year of the Yongle reign, the Prince of Yan swept away the Yuan troops to the north and moved the Ming capital here, thus naming it Beijing and establishing Shuntian Prefecture, which then divided Daxing and Wanping counties. The Qing Dynasty followed the Ming Dynasty without major reforms. In the early years of the Republic of China, Yuan Shikai changed Shuntian Prefecture to Jingzhao. After the successful Northern Expedition of the Kuomintang, the government moved south, renaming it Beiping and designating it as a special municipality. Shortly thereafter, it was changed to an ordinary municipality. Now, with the expansion of the area, its system is being changed back to a special municipality. (December 12th)

Liu Xiang Travels East to Meet Chiang Kai-shek 104

Summons Generals of Five Routes at Wanxian for Instructions

May Visit Authorities in Nanjing After Meeting Chiang

Hankou Dispatch: Liu Xiang, Commander-in-Chief of Bandit Suppression in Sichuan Province, has been planning to travel east to meet Chairman Chiang Kai-shek since resuming his post after a telegram announcement. He intends to report on the situation of remnant bandits in the province, the progress of the armies on all routes in suppression operations, and to seek instructions. Chairman Chiang Kai-shek happened to be on a northern inspection tour, preventing the meeting. However, through exchanged telegrams, they decided to meet in Hankou. Chiang returned south from Shanxi the day before yesterday, only staying in Hankou for a few hours before proceeding to Jiangxi. Liu telegraphed Chiang again for instructions and received Chiang's permission to meet in Nanchang instead. After receiving the telegram, Liu put everything aside and delegated the affairs of the general headquarters and military headquarters to Chief of Staffs Guo and Li respectively. He himself, along with Secretary-General Li Biguo, Chief of the General Staff Zhang Lingjiu, and members of various groups of the headquarters, along with over a hundred guards, departed from Chongqing aboard the Bayu warship at 8:00 AM on the 13th. They arrived in Wanxian that evening. Tang Shizun, Fan Shaozeng, and other front-line generals of the Fifth Route Army, having been summoned by Liu's telegram in advance, rushed from Suixuan to Wanxian to greet him. Liu convened a meeting to discuss in detail the bandit suppression arrangements and command matters during his absence from Sichuan. Liu also gave instructions. Liu stayed in Wanxian for one night and then continued eastward on the original warship. He is expected to arrive in Hankou via Yichang and Shashi on the 15th. He Chenjun received a telegram from Liu on the 13th stating, "Xiang is traveling east by steamer on the first day of the month to meet with the Chairman and seek instructions. Please be informed of the circumstances." He immediately telegraphed Shashi to order Xu Yuanquan to represent him in welcoming Liu and dispatched a plane and a warship to Yichang for standby use. In addition to welcoming Liu in Shashi, Xu also ordered Huang Xin, the brigade commander stationed in Yichang, to warmly welcome Liu upon his arrival in Yichang. Xu will also accompany Liu to Hankou. It is heard that Liu will stay in Hankou for one day to visit Zhang Xueliang, He Chenjun, and Zhang Qun before proceeding to Jiangxi to meet Chiang. If time permits, he will then go to Nanjing to visit the central authorities before returning to Sichuan to supervise the suppression efforts. Liu's representatives in Nanjing and Shanghai, Fu Zhenwu and Deng Wujie, having heard the news of Liu's eastward journey, arrived in Hankou earlier to greet him. Wang Lingji, the former commander of the Fifth Route Army who is residing in Shanghai, will also take the opportunity to come here. (December 13th)

Guangzhou Ferry Bombing Case 105

Bomb Explodes, Three People Injured

Guangzhou Dispatch: The Suichang ferry, which travels between Zhaoqing and Guangzhou, has been operating on the Xijiang route for a long time. However, on the 6th of this month, when the ship arrived at the Guangzhou wharf, an explosion suddenly occurred, injuring three people. It is said that the incident happened because extortion attempts failed, and the criminals hid a bomb on the ship as a threat. When the ship docked at the new wharf on Xidi at about 12:00 AM on the 6th, hundreds of passengers disembarked in good order. When the passengers were almost gone, the owner ordered the crew to clean the cabin. A sailor named Mai Lian found a white iron can containing cigarettes at the bow of the ship. Initially, he thought it was left behind by a passenger, so he took the can to examine it under the light. Just as he was feeling around, there was a flash of light, followed by a loud explosion. The whole ship shook. The crew members rushed over and saw Mai lying in a pool of blood. The five fingers of his left hand and part of his palm had been blown off, a bloody mess, and he was unconscious. A cook named Wu Chihming and a fishmonger named Li Chi were also injured and lying on the ground. Soon after, detectives arrived and searched for the perpetrators. A certain Mr. A, looking flustered, was climbing ashore from the ferry. The police questioned him, and he claimed to be a merchant transporting goods. When questioned by the crew, they all said they were unfamiliar with him. The police considered him suspicious and detained him at the police station for questioning. The three injured were sent to the municipal hospital for treatment. Mai Lian, who was severely injured, had his left arm amputated by the doctor. He is said to be from Nanhai County, 36 years old. Wu Chihming, due to his lighter injuries, was discharged from the hospital the next day after receiving treatment. Fishmonger Li Chi and Mai Lian are still hospitalized. Only a small hole was pierced in the deck of the Suichang ferry's bow, and the hull was not significantly damaged. After the owner reported the case to the authorities as usual, requesting a strict investigation of the perpetrators, the ferry returned to Zhaoqing the next day (7th) as usual, carrying cargo. (December 7th)

Aftermath of the Disaster at Changting 106

Local Security is Gradually Improving

Daily Necessities are Especially Lacking

Shantou Correspondence: After the National Army recovered Changting, Changting refugees returned to their hometowns in droves. The Tinglong Association in Chaozhou Prefecture has set up a refugee registration office. All returnees must register there, be issued a passport, and carry it with them to travel by boat and car free of charge along the way. Changting people living in Chaozhou and Shantou have first sent several people via Shanghang back to Changting to check the actual situation in their hometown after the chaos. Today, a report from Changting merchants stated that when the remnant bandits saw the arrival of the Eastern Route Army, they made a slight resistance in Hang, and then fled to the Jie Ling area of Gucheng. Gucheng was recovered by Li Mo'an on the fourth day. The bandits scattered and fled in several directions. The security in western Fujian is gradually improving. Chen Zhuoru, the administrative commissioner of the Eighth District, has moved his office to Changting City. The headquarters of the Eastern Route Army has moved to Shang Longyan. The highway from Longyan to Liancheng is now open. After the Red bandits retreated, only elderly, weak, disabled men and women remained in the villages and townships. The fields were barren and there was no purchasing power. The silver dollars and copper coins have been completely absorbed by the bandits using counterfeit Farmers and Workers Bank notes. The shops in the market towns have dilapidated walls and roofs, and no doors or windows. In the villages and homes, there are no chickens or dogs, and no complete stoves, water tanks, plates, or bowls. There is a lack of materials, and there is nowhere to buy them. Salt, oil, iron nails, matches, medicines, and all daily necessities must be transported by land from Longyan, making them extremely expensive. It is very difficult for refugees returning to their hometowns to maintain a livelihood. Moreover, the north wind is beginning to blow, piercing the skin and bones like knives. The cotton clothes and bedding of Changting families have long been looted by the bandits. People are using straw or fire for warmth. They desperately hope that the authorities and philanthropists from other places will provide urgent relief. (November 8th)

International Commercial Telegram

November 14th, Special Commercial News from Reuters

Gold and Silver

London Bullion: Today, the price of silver in London is down one-eighth. The spot price is 24.75 pence, and the futures price is 24.875 pence. China sold in the morning, and speculators bought and operated. The closing was calm.

Exchange Rates

British-American: The foreign exchange market in London was quiet today. The British pound has a weak trend against the US dollar. The opening price of the British-American exchange rate was $4.9975, half a cent lower than yesterday's closing price of the American-British exchange rate. It fell another 0.0625 at eleven o'clock, but rose 0.125 at one o'clock in the afternoon to $4.998125. The price remained unchanged at two o'clock.

British-French: The fluctuation of the franc is also very slight. The opening price of the British-French exchange rate was 75.87 francs, 9 pounds lower. It rose 3 pounds at eleven o'clock, and fell 6 pounds at noon, but recovered 6 pounds at one o'clock in the afternoon. The price at two o'clock remained unchanged at 75.90 francs.

American-British: The foreign exchange market in New York was slightly stronger today. The opening price of the American-British exchange rate was $5.00, down 0.25. The American-French exchange rate was 6.56625. The market was quiet in the morning.

Cotton and Wheat

American Cotton: This morning, the New York cotton market opened sluggish, down three pounds from yesterday's closing price. Traders continued to buy as usual. In addition, there were straddle transactions with sellers from the South and buyers from Liverpool. The Agricultural Adjustment Administration advocates increasing the area of ​​underground cotton fields, fearing that if the United States continues to reduce production, Brazil will export cotton to compete with the United States, just as the United States reduces wheat production, while Argentina and Canada export wheat to compete with the United States. However, the bureau does not agree to lower prices and hopes that foreign merchants can use the credit loans arising from silver imports to purchase American cotton.

British Cotton: The Liverpool cotton market also saw lower prices today. At one o'clock in the afternoon, the price for the January futures was 6.58, down four pounds from yesterday's closing.

British Wheat: The Liverpool wheat market fell 0.125 this morning. At one o'clock in the afternoon, the opening price for the February futures was 4 shillings 10.25 pence.

American Wheat: The Chicago wheat market saw a slight drop in futures prices due to favorable weather in the Southwest. Grain prices also fell slightly due to abundant supply. However, the weather in the northern grain belt is currently colder, so the supply may not actually be that plentiful.

Rubber

London: London rubber was stable this morning. At noon, the transaction price for January and March futures was 6.5 pence, the same as yesterday's closing price.

New York: Rubber opened down ten pounds, and then fell another ten pounds. With the price falling, the market turned active and traders bought in.

Securities

New York: Before the opening of the New York stock market, the factors favorable to the market were (1) the Chicago steel mills had increased by one point, reaching 31% of production capacity; (2) the number of railway cars loaded was estimated to be down 12,000 from the previous week, but the increase was still greater than last year; (3) the abolition of foreign exchange restrictions allowed speculators to sharply reduce demand for so-called inflated securities and certain items, but most believe that this measure will ultimately benefit many parties. The factor unfavorable to the market was that during the past week, the market showed a strong trend and there was favorable news for trade, but although the market price had recovered, it ultimately failed to continue and progress, which was disappointing. Today, the stock market opened still active, with slight discrepancies in market price fluctuations. Most stock prices fell slightly. Merchants are unwilling to move forward with the rising trend, so stock market trade is unlikely to have significant fluctuations. The various market prices of New York securities are as follows:

Songjiang

Rice Industry Association Investigates White Racketeering

The local Rice Industry Association has always taken a unified approach to the business operations of its affiliated rice shops, and has established industry rules to ensure compliance with integrity. This county is a rice-producing region, and fluctuations in rice prices are closely related to people's food. Occasional competition is enough to cause the danger of monopoly or disruption of the market. The aforementioned industry rules have been submitted to the county for record. Recently, with Xin Yi taking office, according to regulations, each firm is not allowed to send partners to the countryside to purchase rice, only farmers are allowed to transport it to Songjiang for sale. However, according to recent reports from various parties, some people have violated the industry rules and gone to the countryside to purchase rice at high prices. The Rice Industry Association issued a notice to all its members, reiterating compliance with the industry rules. However, today (14th), a villager named Xu Youfa transported rice to Songjiang and mistakenly reported it to the Jufengchang Rice Mill, claiming that it was purchased by Wu Guihai, who claimed to be from the Yuantong Rice Shop, and had paid a deposit of one yuan. The mill saw that the situation was strange, and after unloading the rice, it was reported to the Rice Industry Association, which investigated the Yuantong Rice Shop for destroying the industry rules and the partner Wu Guihai's illegal rice purchasing behavior. The Yuantong Rice Shop vehemently denied it, so Wu Guihai, the rice purchaser who went to the countryside, was obviously a white racketeer. According to regulations, the association sent a letter to the tooth tax bureau to thoroughly investigate, in order to warn the rest and rectify the industry rules.

Opium Paste Shop to Open Soon

The local Anti-Smoking Committee has approved the application of the Gongji Opium Paste Shop to issue freight documents so that it can go to the warehouse to collect goods and distribute them to opium paste shops in various districts for sale. It is now learned that the operating license for the opium paste shop in the first district has been approved by the provincial capital, Taili. The operating licenses for the opium paste shops in the remaining seven districts have all been issued. Now that the opium paste shop has shipped its goods, the opening date of the opium paste shops in various places should not be far off.

Qingpu

Robbery with Injury in Tangjiaqiao

Last night, more than a dozen bandits suddenly broke into the home of Shen Jinxiang in Tangjiaqiao, District Three, and looted everything. Before leaving, they injured Shen Jinxiang in the head with an iron rod, and his injuries were quite serious. At the same time, they went to the home of Hu Yinlin, who worked as a fortune teller, and thoroughly searched and looted, resulting in irreparable losses. His daughter, Longzhu, a recent widow at home, had her lower body burned with candles by the robbers, which was a terrible sight to behold.

Suzhou

Suzhou Suburbs Begin Winter Defense

The local military, political, and police authorities, considering that winter defense is imminent and defense is tight, have specially organized a Winter Defense Committee, which is scheduled to begin winter defense today (15th). The various departments of the Second District of the Water Police and the Seventh Battalion of the Security Corps have been ordered to go to the countryside and be stationed at key points along Taihu Lake, and from time to time, they will jointly conduct drills with the local military and police. The defense of the urban area is the responsibility of the Public Security Bureau and the Chamber of Commerce. Starting last night, they are all on duty.

Opium Paste Shops and Smoking Dens Begin Operations

The Wu County Anti-Smoking Association has completed the registration of smokers, and issued Category A smoker licenses yesterday (14th) and Category B smoker licenses today. The various opium paste shops and smoking dens will begin operations at the same time.

Wuxi

Universal Reduction of Land Tax by Two Percent Throughout the County

This year, the county experienced a drought. The county government sent officials to various villages and towns to survey the autumn crops, and also requested the Civil and Financial Affairs Departments to send officials to re-survey. At the same time, the county government submitted the drought situation to the Finance Department for review and decision. It was calculated that there were more than 148,160 acres of completely barren land with no harvest, and a request was made for a universal reduction of 13 percent. It is now learned that after receiving the report, the Finance Department proposed to the Provincial Government Committee to amend the seventh article of the "Measures for Surveying and Reporting Disasters and Deficiencies" regarding the exemption of gold and barren land tax, and issued a circular for compliance. It should be handled in accordance with the amended article and must not be unlimited. Therefore, yesterday, it specially instructed Strict County Magistrate of the county to thoroughly investigate and carefully screen the land, separately categorizing increases and decreases. The highest limit should be no more than a two percent reduction in the total harvest of the entire county, including the completely barren land, and an actual tax collection of eight percent must be determined before a decision can be made.

Kidnappers from Yixing Arrested in Wuxi

The Public Security Bureau of Yixing County recently arrested twelve kidnappers. According to their confessions, there were still accomplices named Shi Zuoqing and Shi Du氏 who were hiding in Ximen, Wuxi. The Bureau immediately sent a constable with a warrant to Wuxi and directly reported to the local Public Security Bureau, requesting them to send personnel to assist in the arrest. After Chen, the Bureau Chief, approved the letter, he ordered Zhong Jihe, the captain of the Criminal Investigation Team, to send Zhang Biao, an investigator, to arrest the suspects at the address. They arrested Shi Zuoqing and his wife in a workshop outside Ximen and temporarily detained them at the Bureau. Yesterday, investigators from Yi County came to Wuxi to take them back for interrogation.

Changzhou

Gang Leader from Yixing Arrested in Changzhou

Zhong Jingcheng, the County Magistrate and Public Security Bureau Chief of Yixing County, arrested twelve kidnappers on the 12th, and seized three pistols. According to their confessions, gang leader Xu Jinquan and accomplice Zhang Jinsheng were hiding in Changzhou. He immediately sent Patrol Officer Xu Runzhi and Detective Pan Jie of the Criminal Investigation Team, each carrying weapons and in disguise, to Changzhou to arrest them overnight, and sent a letter to the Changzhou Branch Security Bureau for assistance. Director Xu immediately sent a captain of the motorcycle team and Constable Zhu Maozhong to arrest gang leader Xu Jinquan at his residence, and seized a number of stolen goods. He also arrested the suspect Zhang Jinsheng at the Changle Inn on Taiping Lane in Ximen. After a preliminary interrogation at the Bureau, they were handed over to the police from Yixing for interrogation.

Yangzhou

Inaugural Meeting of the Canal Engineering Bureau Evaluation Council

After the Jiangbei Canal Engineering Bureau was re-established in Yangzhou, Director Xu believed that if the evaluation councils previously organized in the Xu, Hai, Huai, and Yang prefectures under its jurisdiction were not also re-established, it would be insufficient to gather opinions and broaden benefits. Therefore, he submitted a request to the Provincial Government to continue to appoint local gentry who were familiar with water conservancy in each county, and schedule a meeting to discuss improvements. The Provincial Government approved the request. The meeting was scheduled for the 14th and 15th of this month. As of the 13th, those who had arrived to report included Zhou Yiren from Jiangdu, Han Guojun from Taixian, Ma Shijie from Gaoyou, Shi Jinsheng from Xinghua, Xu Xinwu from Yizheng, Feng Xiaoting from Pei County, Ding Ximin from Xiao County, Liu Shulun from Suqian, Bei Yunqi from Suining, Feng Beiying from Pi County, Wu Tongju from Guanyun, Xu Baoyu from Muyang, Chen Deru from Siyang, Hao Xingheng from Yancheng, and Chen Bomeng from Funing, totaling sixteen people. The counties that had not arrived included Dong Xueshan from Feng County, Zhang Yunsheng from Tongshan, Sun Zhuping from Dangshan, Xu Changqing from Ganyu, Tian Lujian from Huai'an, Wang Shuxiang from Huaiyin, Luo Dongfu from Lianshui, and Wang Lianfen from Dongtai, totaling eight people. The opening ceremony and tea party were held at 2:00 pm on the 14th. The meeting period was from morning to night on the 15th. In addition to the twelve project proposals compiled by the Canal Engineering Bureau and the reports on the past engineering conditions and the actual estimated expenses for each project, the proposals submitted to the council included Feng Beiying's proposal that the breach in the Fengmao section of the Pi County Canal should be repaired with dikes and gates to prevent Shen flooding, and Shi Wuyong's proposal that after the construction of the Wangzhu two port gates, the tide seems to be defensible, but there is no certainty whether the South Fifth Salt Field will backflow, and it is proposed to continue to manage the Dingxiaocao three gate dams to maintain water conservancy.

Nantong

Random Inspection of Baojia in Six Counties of the Nantong Region

The third phase of Baojia work in the six counties of the Nantong region has been completed. After inspection and correction by the Commissioner's Office, Sun Xiayun was sent by the Department of Civil Affairs to Nantong, Rugao, Jingjiang, and Du Pinsan was sent to Haimen, Chongming, and Qidong for random inspections.

Merger of Postal and Telegraph Bureaus

The Nantong Postal and Telegraph Bureaus have been ordered by the Ministry of Communications to merge on the 15th of this month. The bureau will be located in the new market town south of the city.

Haimen

Autumn Harvest Fixed at 85 Percent

Since the summer of this year, the county has experienced a prolonged drought, and the crops have withered, resulting in an autumn harvest of less than 40 percent. After the county government reported to the Provincial Department and sent personnel to inspect, it reported 70 percent. Local people believed that the people's strength could not bear the burden, and they successively submitted requests for reduction. However, the Department of Finance still considered the number too small and ordered the county to increase it appropriately. The county government then convened a meeting of representatives from various agencies and groups, who all said that the disaster situation this year was extremely severe and unprecedented in a century. In order to balance the interests of the country and the people, it was reluctantly proposed to collect 60 percent and submit it to the Provincial Department for approval. Yesterday (11th), an telegram was received from the Department of Finance, stating that the autumn harvest in the county was not a major disaster and that the request could not be approved. According to the proposals of the autumn survey committee, 15 percent was added to fix the collection at 85 percent. Local officials were shocked by the news and held a meeting that night to jointly submit a request for reduction and send representatives to the province to petition.

Cai Hongsheng's Wife Kidnapped

At about 8:00 pm the day before yesterday, seven or eight bandits speaking with mixed accents and each holding a box gun suddenly came to the home of Cai Hongsheng, a wealthy household in Fanglin Township, District Four, broke down the door and searched at will. At the time, Cai was out and not at home. The bandits twisted and beat Cai's wife, Chen, and forced her to hand over silver dollars, but failed. They then kidnapped her and left. Yesterday, Cai reported to the District Office, which forwarded the report to the County Government for investigation.

Jiashan

Prison Officer Punished for Accepting Bribes

Hu Baorong, a clerk in the county prison from Shaoxing, and Lu Zian, a fireman in the Second Detention Center, were jointly accused of bribery by four inmates, Huang Songdu, Wang Jianqing, etc. After investigation, it was confirmed to be true. Hu Baorong was released on bail, and Lu Zian was detained. Later, the prosecutor filed a public prosecution, and the court sentenced them each to four years of imprisonment.

Local News

The Remains of Our Newspaper's General Manager Shi Were Transported to Shanghai Yesterday 107

The Encoffining Ceremony Will Be Held Tomorrow Afternoon

Condolences Received from All Sectors at Home and Abroad

Our newspaper's General Manager, Mr. Shi Liangcai, accompanied by his wife, son, niece, and his son Yonggeng's classmate, Deng Zuxun, and others, departed from Qiushui Villa in West Lake at approximately 2:00 pm the day before yesterday (the 13th) in his own car, number 5599, driven by the chauffeur Huang Jincai, to return to Shanghai via the Shanghai-Hangzhou Highway. However, at approximately 3:00 pm, when the car was passing Wengjiabu at Dazhakou, the intersection of Hangzhou and Haining counties, a Buick car was discovered ahead. Six or seven thugs blocked the road and fired box cannons head-on. The chauffeur and Deng Zuxun were killed on the spot. Although General Manager Shi immediately got out of the car and fled upon seeing the opportunity, he was ultimately killed by the thugs due to his age and lack of strength. Mrs. Shi was injured in a fall while fleeing, and her niece was also hit by a bullet in her left leg when bullets were flying. Only his son, Yonggeng, got out of the car and ran backward as fast as he could when the thugs were shooting the chauffeur and Deng. Although three thugs followed closely behind and fired remotely, he managed to avoid disaster due to his speed. Seeing that their goal had been achieved, the thugs immediately took their original car and fled towards Hangzhou. Afterwards, Yonggeng requested that a car be sent from the Jianqiao Aviation School to the scene of the incident, and Mrs. Shi and her niece were rescued back to Hangzhou for medical treatment. After arriving in Hangzhou, the Zhejiang Provincial Government and the Municipal Government, together with the Hangzhou County Local Court, dispatched cars late at night to transport the three bodies back to Hangzhou. Shanghai also dispatched personnel that night and the hearse from the Wan Gu Funeral Home rushed to Hangzhou overnight to transport the bodies back to Shanghai, arriving at the residence on Hartung Road yesterday afternoon at 4:30 pm to prepare for the funeral. The police authorities of Zhejiang and Shanghai are now making every effort to investigate the murderers. Mrs. Shi and her son Yonggeng also arrived in Shanghai yesterday afternoon at 8:00 pm to handle all the post-mortem arrangements. The detailed circumstances of this incident are recorded in detail below.

The Arrival of Mr. Shi Liangcai's Remains at the Residence (Zhu Shunlin)

Head-on Shooting

According to our reporter's accurate investigation, the detailed circumstances of the encounter are supplemented as follows: At approximately 2:00 pm on the 13th, Mr. Shi and his wife, son Yonggeng, and others took their own car from Hangzhou and returned to Shanghai along the Shanghai-Hangzhou Highway. There were a total of six people in the car. The chauffeur, Huang Jincai, Yonggeng's classmate, Deng Zuxun, and Yonggeng were sitting in the front row, while Mr. Shi and his wife and the third young lady were in the car compartment. At approximately 3:00 pm, the car passed Qiaosi and reached about two li north of Wengjiabu Station. From a distance, they saw a Buick car, number Jingzi 72, model 1929, parked on the side of the road. Six or seven men in black were standing next to the car, and their attitude was very suspicious. At that time, the car was traveling very fast. When they were more than ten feet away, they suddenly heard a whistle. The six or seven thugs next to the car all took out box cannons and fired at the Shi's car head-on.

Three Bandits Relentlessly Pursue

The chauffeur, Huang Jincai, seeing the disaster, quickly leaned over to hide while stepping on the brakes. Due to the speed of the car, there was a sudden loud noise, and the car stopped right where the thugs were standing. At that moment, bullets were flying, and the front windshield shattered into pieces. Deng Zuxun, a classmate next to the chauffeur, was also extremely frightened and prostrated. At this critical moment, Yonggeng saw the imminent danger, quickly opened the car door and jumped out, turning around and running along the highway towards Hangzhou. Three bandits chased after him, firing dozens of shots, none of which hit him. Yonggeng was wearing a coat, which made running very difficult. He quickly took off his coat midway and threw it into the field, rushing forward for his life. Two of the three bandits ran out of strength and fell behind, with only one bandit pursuing relentlessly, but no longer firing. It seemed that the bullets had run out. After a while, Yonggeng was also exhausted. The last bandit had chased him to his back. In desperation, Yonggeng suddenly turned around and asked why he was being chased relentlessly. The bandit replied, "You come with me," and tried his best to pull the trigger, but the bullet did not come out. Then he grabbed Yonggeng's wrist. Yonggeng shook him off with force and grabbed the barrel of the box cannon he was holding. The bandit also tried to snatch it with force. The barrel was slippery, and it was eventually taken away. The barrel had triangular spikes, causing Yonggeng's palm to be injured and bleeding profusely. Seeing that it was not easy to deal with, the bandit turned around and fled. Yonggeng feared that the bandit would reunite with his accomplices and come back, so he reluctantly ran to Wengjiabu Station to call for help.

Shot in Vital Parts

At the same time, Mr. Shi, his wife, and the third young lady opened the right car door and fled, going downhill towards the countryside. Two bandits chased Mr. Shi and others. After walking about half a li, Mr. Shi fled into the home of a farmer surnamed Shen. One bandit tracked him inside, while the other bandit went around to the back door to wait. When Mr. Shi rushed out of the back door, he was shot in the foot by the bandit. He still endured the pain and crawled a few steps to a dry small pond, where he fell to the ground. The two bandits fired two more shots at his head, one entering the brain through the mouth and the other entering through the left ear, both hitting vital parts, and he died immediately. As for the third young lady, she was shot in the leg and fell to the side of the road. One bandit was about to shoot her again, but stopped after she begged for mercy. Mrs. Shi was injured when she rolled down the slope. After the bandits left in the car, the third young lady shouted loudly to the villagers for help, and they were helped to rest in a farmer's home.

Bandit Car Speeding Away

Yonggeng, with effort, ran to Wengjiabu Station, already too tired to move. At that time, the villagers were asking questions in panic, inquiring about the details of the encounter. As they were talking, they saw the bandit car speeding towards Hangzhou from a distance. Yonggeng was shocked, thinking that the bandits were coming to attack, and ran away to the countryside. In the blink of an eye, the bandit car passed by and drove away. Yonggeng's frightened soul had just settled, and he returned to the station. He telegraphed Qiaosi Station from the station, and Yonggeng was carried to Jianqiao Airfield by a villager in a small cart. He met the instructors of the Aviation School and told them the details. The instructors immediately telegraphed to all parties to inform them, and sent more than a dozen armed guards to accompany Yonggeng to the scene of the incident for rescue. The policemen of the Public Security Bureau had already arrived after the telephone report from the third young lady, and learned that Mr. Shi, Deng Zuxun, and the chauffeur had been killed. The ambulance from the Aviation School then transported the injured Mrs. Shi and the third young lady to Hangzhou, and Yonggeng also went along. After the bodies of Mr. Shi and others underwent forensic examination procedures, they were transported back to Hangzhou until approximately 4:00 am yesterday.

Body Transported to Shanghai

After receiving the report the night before, Mr. Ma Yinliang, the manager of our newspaper, immediately gathered important staff of the newspaper at the Shi's residence to discuss all the post-mortem arrangements with the family. At 8:30 pm, he took three cars, accompanied by Huang Yanqing, Huang Zijian, Huang Renzhi, and Wang Yingbin from the General Management Office, and at the same time instructed the Wan Gu Funeral Home to send a foreigner and a hearse to Hangzhou to transport the body back to Shanghai. After arriving in Hangzhou at 3:00 am yesterday, he went to Tingyun Villa, where the foreigner washed Mr. Shi's body and gave him an embalming injection. Then, together with the bodies of Deng Zuxun and Zhang Jincai, he set off for Shanghai at 8:00 am yesterday, arriving at the Wan Gu Funeral Home on Jiaozhou Road at 1:30 pm. The technicians of the funeral home performed surgery to wash and make up the body, and then at approximately 5:00 pm, the body was transported by the hearse to the residence on Hartung Road. Then, two foreigners from the funeral home moved the body to the prepared memorial seat in the old house's hall.

Family Members Mourn

After the body was placed, the red satin covering the face was removed by the foreigners. At this time, all the men, women, young and old of the family surrounded the body and mourned bitterly, and all the old friends and colleagues of the newspaper also wept and cried uncontrollably. The body of Mr. Shi, after being made up by the technicians, although his face was pale, still seemed to have a slight smile, but his ears were slightly purple, and his mouth and eyes were closed as if he were asleep.

Guests Sign Their Names

Those who went to the Shi's residence yesterday afternoon to offer condolences included Wu Tiecheng, Wang Zhengting, Chen Taoyi, Zhu Qinglan, Pan Gongzhan, Yang Hu, Du Yuesheng, Wu Xingya, Huang Renzhi, Chen Lengxue, Qian Xinzhi, Zhang Zhuping, Wu Yunqi, Chen Guangfu, Wang Boqi, Yan Fuqing, Li Dachao, Mu Ouchu, Guo Shun, Lin Kanghou, and many others, as well as all the staff and workers of our newspaper, who all went to pay their respects to the deceased, and were all saddened to tears. They all bowed to the spirit. In addition, Takeshi Kinoshita, the Shanghai correspondent of the Osaka Asahi Shimbun, and Hakuhaku Hata, the president of the Shanghai Daily, personally came to the newspaper to leave their business cards to express their condolences.

Family Members Return to Shanghai

Mrs. Shi and her son Yonggeng took the Shanghai-Hangzhou train to Shanghai at 2:00 pm yesterday. When Yonggeng and others came to Shanghai, they were closely protected by road police and bodyguards to prevent accidents. They arrived safely at the residence at 7:30 pm in the evening. Mrs. Shi suffered severe hemoptysis due to the shock during the incident, so she was examined by a doctor after arriving at the residence. Ms. Shen Lijuan, the niece who was also injured at the same time the day before yesterday, is currently staying temporarily at Guangji Hospital in Hangzhou, and will return to Shanghai after she recovers from her injuries. The bodies of Deng Zuxun and Huang Jincai were transported to Shanghai at the same time as Mr. Shi's body and are scheduled to be encoffined tomorrow at the Chinese Funeral Home. The body of the chauffeur, Jincai, will be encoffined at the Wan Gu Funeral Home.

Encoffining Ceremony Tomorrow

The family has decided to hold the encoffining ceremony at 2:00 pm on the 16th of this month, and then schedule the memorial service and funeral. The encoffining location will be held in the garden of the Shi's residence. A large tent was set up overnight last night for use. The Shi's residence formally announced the obituary to relatives and friends last night.

Official Pursuit of the Culprits

After the incident, the Hangzhou Public Security Bureau immediately dispatched police to rigorously pursue and apprehend the perpetrators. However, the thugs had already escaped without a trace, making it impossible to capture them. Efforts are currently underway to apprehend them. Furthermore, upon receiving the information, the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau has dispatched a large number of detectives and police officers to conduct investigations and check pedestrians at major transportation routes and stations. Also, because the license plate of the car used by the thugs was "Jingshi 72," the Beijing Municipal Public Security Bureau has been specifically requested via telegram to thoroughly investigate in order to apprehend the culprits and bring them to justice.

Eyewitness Account by a Westerner

On the afternoon of the incident, a foreign electrical engineer from this city, Mr. Stephen Heller, was also returning to Shanghai from Hangzhou. His car passed the border between Haining and Hangzhou just minutes after Mr. Shi was murdered. According to Mr. Stephen: "I left Hangzhou at 3 PM yesterday. There were not many vehicles on the road, so I was driving very fast. After driving fifteen miles (about one mile from Jianqiao Aviation School), I saw a car stopped by the side of the road, surrounded by many soldiers and civilians. The road was blocked. I got out of the car." The car stopped by the side of the road was a brand-new Studebaker private car. The two front lights were on, but the third front light had been destroyed. The front wheels and tires had also been punctured. I looked into the car, and a terrifying scene immediately came into view. The driver and another young man (namely, Deng) were lying stiffly in the front seat, bleeding profusely. The seat cushions were soaked in blood. There was also a lot of blood on the road. At this time, doctors from Hangzhou had arrived at the scene to provide medical attention. I inspected the car again and saw that the wheels had been damaged, but the car body was still intact. The details of the incident varied from person to person. According to some, a car drove past the Studebaker car, first puncturing the tires, then killing the driver, and forcing the car to stop. I was taking pictures at this time, and laborers were carrying another body. I then got back in my car and returned to Shanghai.

The Niece's Injuries

A telegram from Hangzhou stated that the niece, Ms. Shen Lijuan, who is being treated at Guangji Hospital, had a bullet removed from her left leg muscle yesterday. Her condition has gradually returned to normal, and she is able to walk on her own today. However, the doctors have instructed her to rest due to the deep shock she experienced. She is expected to be discharged from the hospital in about two months.

Apprehension of a Suspect

A telegram from Hangzhou stated that at 1 PM today (the 14th), railway police at Zhuji Station on the Hangzhou-Jiangshan Railway apprehended a suspect in the Shi case, named Tang Baoying. He was found to be carrying a handgun. He is currently detained at the county Public Security Bureau and will be escorted to Hangzhou tomorrow morning (today). Since the case occurred, the Provincial Public Security Bureau has telegraphed Beijing to inquire about the owner of the car with license plate "Jingshi 72." According to a reply telegram from the Beijing Municipal Public Works Bureau, the car with license plate "72" belongs to the Yanye Bank and is still in Nanjing. Furthermore, according to a Nanjing telegram from the Central News Agency on the 14th, the car used by the thugs had a "Jing" license plate number 72 for test vehicles. A reporter from the Central News Agency specifically inquired with the Beijing Public Works Bureau on the morning of the 14th. According to the staff member in charge of car license plates, the Beijing government issues five types of car license plates: (1) black plate with white characters for private cars; (2) white plate with black characters for commercial vehicles; (3) white plate with a blue diagonal stripe and red characters for test vehicles; (4) yellow plate with black characters for commercial trucks; and (5) black plate with yellow characters for private trucks. Of these five types, only the black plate for private cars has the number "72." The other four types do not. The black plate number 72 belongs to the Yanye Bank in this city. This morning, the 14th, the car and the driver were brought to the municipal government for verification. It was learned that the car had not left Beijing in the past two days. The reporter then asked if the test vehicle license plate number 27 had been issued. After checking, the staff member showed the reporter the license plate, stating that the number had not been issued recently. As for the test vehicle license plate number 72, there is no such number at all.

Telegram of Condolences and Congratulations from 183 Trade Associations 109

The New Voice News Agency reported that recent military operations to suppress bandits have achieved successive victories, and the bandit stronghold in Ruijin has been recaptured. 183 trade associations in this city, including the silk and satin industry, cotton cloth industry, paper industry, rice industry, sugar industry, cinder industry, timber industry, woolen industry, and dried goods industry, have jointly sent a telegram to Chairman Chiang and General Commander Chiang Dingwen of the Eastern Route Army and Commander Li Mo'an of the 10th Division, expressing their condolences and congratulations. The text of the telegram is as follows: "Urgent National Matter, to Chairman Chiang, forwarded by the Nanchang Headquarters; and to General Commanders Jiang Ming and Li Mo'an of the Eastern Route Army and Commander Li Mo'an of the 10th Division, as an aid to understanding: The scourge of the Red Bandits has affected several provinces, devastating rural areas and endangering the nation. Fortunately, Your Excellencies have demonstrated foresight and made the great decision to first pacify the country and then resist foreign aggression, exterminating those bandits to secure the foundation of the nation. Since taking command, the officers and soldiers have been dedicated, and the bandit forces have crumbled before the righteous banner. Recently, Ruijin and other places have been recaptured. The bandit nest has been destroyed, and the remaining bandits are terrified. Hearing of this from afar, we are overjoyed. Considering Your Excellencies' tireless efforts day and night, and the officers and soldiers' dedication on the front lines, they have undoubtedly endured hardship. However, the safety of the Party and the nation depends on this. We hope you will seize the opportunity to continue the suppression and achieve complete success. As the army advances, the people will be revitalized. We first send this telegram of condolence and extend our heartfelt wishes. The silk and satin industry, cotton cloth industry, paper industry, rice industry, sugar industry, cinder industry, timber industry, woolen industry, and dried goods industry, 183 trade associations of Shanghai, respectfully, Cold."

Rice Industry Leaders Discuss Grain Panic in This City 110

Estimated Inventory Can Ensure a Safe Passage This Year

Eager to Purchase Imported Rice, but Difficult to Maintain Low Prices Due to Heavy Taxes

The New Voice News Agency reported that this year's widespread drought in various parts of our country has led to an unprecedented grain panic, with soaring prices. Yesterday, reporters from the New Voice News Agency specially visited Mr. Gu Xinyi and Mr. Jiang Shizhi, leaders of the grain industry in this city, who kindly gave interviews, which are recorded below.

Production Halved, Supply Cannot Meet Demand

According to Mr. Gu Xinyi, this year, the rice-producing areas of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Jiangxi, and Anhui provinces have been affected by drought, resulting in a sharp decline in production. Jiangsu's output is half of what it was in previous years, Zhejiang's is only 40%, and Jiangxi's is the same. Anhui is better than Zhejiang and Jiangxi, with an average harvest of only 50%. Therefore, the province, which usually has a surplus of food, is now experiencing a fear of supply not meeting demand.

Ordered 1.5 Million Bags of Imported Rice

Due to the supply not meeting the demand, the rice industry and speculative financial industry have successively ordered imported rice from Saigon, Rangoon, and Bangkok, totaling over 1.5 million bags to date. Besides the 250,000 bags that have already been imported, there are another 150,000 bags scheduled to be imported in November and December. The rest are futures contracts for the first half of the new year, mainly sold to Zhejiang, Jiangsu, Jiangxi, and other places for disaster prevention and military needs. Sales in Shanghai are only a small portion.

Drought Wreaks Havoc, Rice Ears Shrivel

Wuxi, Changshu, Suzhou, Songjiang, Qingpu, and Zhujiajiao in Jiangsu, and Jiaxing, Ningbo, Jiashan, and other places in Zhejiang, were originally rice-producing areas. Due to the prolonged drought, coupled with shriveled rice ears (normally, every 100 catties of grain can yield 5 dou of rice, but now it only yields a little over 4 dou), the harvest is also reduced. As a result, the price of new rice, which was expected to fall, remains stubbornly high. Some merchants in Shanghai are even buying imported rice to prevent a shortage of local sales.

No Worries This Year, Panic Next Year

Mr. Gu also said that the reason for the high rice prices in Shanghai is mainly due to the drought, as well as farmers hoarding grain. In previous years, they would sell off all their grain, but now they only sell a small portion. Businesses hoard it, waiting for a good price. They also reduce the amount transported to Shanghai. In addition, there are many speculators who buy as much as possible, manipulating the market, making it difficult for prices to fall. Currently, the sales in Shanghai and the amount arriving from the surrounding countryside can offset each other. There are 100,000 dan of imported rice in storage, 30,000 dan of local rice in the South City, and 40,000 dan in the North City. The people's food supply this year is guaranteed, but next year, a panic is inevitable.

Flour Shortage, Imported Wheat Transactions

As for flour, the price has been rising recently due to the shortage of goods. The Hua Feng Flour Mill purchased two ships of imported wheat from Argentina yesterday, at a price of 4.80 yuan per 100 catties. The Li Xin Flour Mill ordered one ship from Australia, at a price of 9 yuan per 100 catties, totaling 25,000 tons. The Australian goods are expected to be shipped to Shanghai around December 2nd, and the Argentine goods will arrive in Shanghai in mid-January next year. It is understood that the flour industry will continue to place orders to prevent a market shortage.

Sparse Inventory in Surrounding Countryside, Less Than Half Sufficient

According to Jiang Shizhi, the inventory in the surrounding countryside is very low. Wuxi alone has over 100,000 dan of stored old rice, 100,000 dan of new rice, and 40,000 dan of japonica rice. In total, Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces have 1 million dan of rice in stock (excluding what is harvested). Based on the production and sales of the two provinces, this is less than half sufficient. Hunan province, after meeting its own sales needs, has a surplus that can offset a quarter of the shortage in the two provinces. As for Anhui province, it also has a surplus. In the past, it was purchased from Guangdong, but since the seizure of relief rice at Dashengguan, the transportation of Anhui rice to Guangdong has ceased because of overestimation and overtaxation.

Guangdong Procures Imported Rice with Half the Tax, Ships It to Shanghai

Mr. Jiang also said that as for purchasing imported rice, the Shanghai rice industry had requested the government to reduce import taxes but was unsuccessful. Every stone is taxed at 3.4 yuan, which, combined with the cost, makes it unprofitable to sell, making it difficult to lower rice prices. Guangdong province procures Saigon rice with only half the tax, so merchants in Guangdong are frantically purchasing imported rice and plan to ship it to Shanghai to avoid taxes. It is said that over 100,000 stones are already en route. According to this year's situation, except for Jiangbei, which is self-sufficient, the shortfall in Jiangnan can be safely overcome.

Key to Adjusting People's Food Supply Lies in Taxes

Although more than one million stones of imported rice will be imported next year, the vast drought-stricken areas mean that this is just a drop in the bucket and not enough to distribute. The future is worrisome. If the government can halve or exempt the import tax on imported rice, rice merchants can order as much imported rice as possible to suppress the panic of domestic rice and regulate the people's food supply. Therefore, the important key to whether there will be a rice shortage next year depends entirely on whether the government can exempt and reduce taxes.

The 20 million yuan of Zhejiang Local Public Bonds issued on October 1st of the 23rd year of the Republic of China will soon have the bond certificates printed. The Late Police Commissioner Wen Hongen Received His Final Burial Yesterday 113

Many Guests Attended to Offer Condolences

The Coffin Was Temporarily Placed in Guangdong Hospital

Commissioner Wen Hongen of the Shanghai Municipal Police Bureau, having overworked due to official duties and fallen ill, passed away at the Shanghai West Sanatorium on the afternoon of the 12th. The body was moved to the China Funeral Home on Hague Road for the final burial. High-ranking officials from Beijing and Shanghai, the military, and the government, leaders from all walks of life in this city, representatives from social groups, foreign dignitaries, and foreign guests all went to offer condolences after learning of the news. The situation has been recorded in previous reports. Yesterday at 2:30 PM, the final burial was held, and the number of guests was even more crowded. There was a constant stream of plain white cars on Hague Road. The autumn wind made the atmosphere more bleak. Details are recorded below:

Final Burial Yesterday Afternoon 114

At 10 AM, the family dressed Mr. Wen's body in civil official attire. Photos were taken at 1 PM and moved to the hall to set up the memorial tablet. Guests from all walks of life, such as Xu Fu, Chen Ce, Zeng Zesheng, Liao Lanting, Wu Tiecheng, Xu Xueyu, Wang Changchun, Li Dachao, Chen Kecheng, Wu Zhihao, Yang Hu, Yuan Lianghua, Yan Fuqing, Shen Gao, Wu Kaixian, Zheng Hongnian, Gan Hailan, Ge Zhenyu, Yu Hongjun, Wang Xiaolai, Pan Gongzhan, Wu Shaozeng, Shen Junru, Li Tingan, Wu Xingya, He Dekui, Xu Peihuang, as well as Kamitani Kisaburo, Yokohira Taro, the Japanese Associations, representatives from the Shanghai Japanese Residents Association, the various district defense corps fire brigades, and officers from various public security sub-bureaus, over a thousand people, paid their respects in turn at the memorial. At 2:30 PM, the final burial was held, with the police band playing mournful music.

[Image] Photo of Commissioner Wen's Burial (Taken by Qichang)

A Glimpse of the Funeral Hall 115

The hall was decorated with white couplets and plaques. Wreaths from Song Ziwen, Kong Xiangxi, Sun Ke, Ma Chaojun, Sato, Tang Haian, Wang Zhengting, Xu Shiying, Lu Wenlan, Du Yong, Wang Jingqi, the Guangdong Fellow Villagers Association, and various other groups filled the hall.

Temporary Placement in the Funeral Home 116

At 6 PM, Mr. Wen's coffin was transported by a special car from the China Funeral Home to the Guangdong Hospital in Zhabei for temporary placement. The funeral procession was led by a band, followed by family and friends.

Merits During His Lifetime 117

After the tragic news of Mr. Wen's death spread, social groups, merchants, and the public all mourned deeply. This was because Mr. Wen was diligent in his service, upheld integrity, and only served for two years and three months. However, he reformed the police administration with remarkable achievements. The peace and order of the locality was something rarely seen in recent years. As for police reforms, the most prominent ones included the reform of the sub-bureaus, the erection of police monuments, the construction of police cemeteries, the restoration of police training schools, the replenishment of weapons, the addition of uniforms, the creation of police death relief and employee death benefits, the establishment of police savings, and the construction of a new headquarters. All of these facilities were completed during Mr. Wen's tenure. He was truly meritorious. Many police officers in the bureau were moved to tears upon hearing the tragic news, which shows how deeply Mr. Wen's life affected people.

Last Will and Testament 118

According to Mr. Wen’s relatives and friends speaking with a reporter, Director Wen was of a robust constitution. This past autumn, he initially suffered from dysentery, followed by a relapse of old ailments. He was immediately admitted to a Chinese-Western sanatorium for treatment. He improved slightly half a month prior, and went to a sanatorium in West Shanghai to recuperate. Unexpectedly, his condition worsened, ultimately leading to his demise, which is deeply regretted. Before his passing, he was still mentally lucid. Mayor Wu, Naval Department Director Chen Ce, his uncle Wen, Division Commander Chao Ji, Chief Secretary Sun Zhongying, Section Chief Lin Wenquan, and family members were all at his side. Mr. Wen was still able to bid them farewell one by one. He first expressed his gratitude for Mayor Wu’s support and kindness throughout his life, expressing regret that he was unable to repay this kindness, which he considered a great regret. He repeatedly urged his younger siblings to carry on his legacy, follow the leadership of their predecessors, and alleviate the national crisis. Finally, he said to his uncle, Division Commander Wen Chaoji, and his close friend Chen Ce, "I am a revolutionary soldier and have long dedicated myself to the country. Although I have been wounded many times, unfortunately, I will not die on the battlefield, but instead will die in bed, which is not my wish. Currently, the national crisis has not been resolved, lost territories have not been recovered, and the communist bandits have not been completely annihilated, which is the responsibility of those who survive," and so on. Even as he spoke to this point, his spirit did not wane. He continued to instruct his family on household matters in an orderly fashion. Finally, he instructed Chief Secretary Sun and Section Chief Lin, as well as his family, to have his handwritten "Zhu Zi's Family Precepts" printed in collotype and sent to relatives, friends, and colleagues as a memento. He was able to arrange such trivial matters one by one, which is quite rare. His concern for national affairs and constant thoughts of saving the country are particularly thought-provoking.

Condolence Messages from All Quarters 119

Following the death of Mr. Wen, numerous condolence telegrams arrived. Xie Shou Kang, former Minister to Belgium and current member of the Legislative Yuan, telegraphed, "To the Shanghai Public Security Bureau, Mr. Wen Hua Lei: I was saddened to hear of the passing of Director Duiting. Please convey my condolences to his sister-in-law and nephews. Respectfully, Xie Shou Kang." Also, the Nanjing Qiongyai Association in Beijing telegraphed, "To the Shanghai Public Security Bureau, condolences to the family of Director Wen: I was shocked to read in the newspaper that Director Wen had passed away due to illness. We deeply mourn his passing. This association respectfully sends its condolences on behalf of all the Qiongyai people in Beijing. Respectfully, Qiongyai Association in Beijing." Furthermore, Mr. Arnold, the Chairman of the Shanghai Municipal Council, sent a letter to Mayor Wu yesterday (the 14th) expressing condolences on the death of Director Wen Hongen. The letter stated, "Director Wen has worked steadily and cooperatively for the common interests of the two districts for two years. All the directors and staff of the Municipal Council greatly admire him. We are deeply saddened by his sudden passing. On behalf of the Municipal Council, we extend our condolences to his family."

Shanghai Will Become a World-Famous City 122

According to the "North China Daily News," Colonel Fairbank, former president of the International Olympic Games, is an inventor and economist. He invented a machine gun that can write symbols in the air, like a person signing a commemorative album. He recently discussed military preparations and current issues with colleagues. Mr. Fairbank's invention is a type of sound detector that was used during the European War to locate the gathering of artillery units and the location of ships. When asked about his machine gun yesterday, Mr. Fairbank replied that each cannon has a different sound and can be identified by the waves it emits on the telegraph wire. After discussing this, Mr. Fairbank discussed economic issues with the guests, stating that even if Shanghai does not become the largest city in the world in fifty years, it will become one of the world's most famous cities.

Banking Association Submits Opinions on the Banking Law to the Ministry 123

Chen Guangfu and Others Meet with the Director of the Currency Department to Present Them in Person

The Ministry of Finance Promises to Forward the Opinions to the Legislative Yuan

According to the "Newspaper," the Shanghai Banking Association and the Banking Law Research Association have concluded their work. The research findings, along with supporting reasons, total about eleven or twelve articles. Among them, three or four are the most important [the rest are common]. In particular, Article 5 of the Banking Law, which states that "shareholders of limited liability companies, and limited and joint-stock companies, shall be liable for twice the amount of their subscribed shares," is the most important. This has now been approved by the 58th Executive Committee of the Banking Association and was submitted to the Legislative Yuan's Ministry of Finance the night before yesterday, offering their opinions and requesting adoption. Chen Guangfu, Chairman of the Banking Association, and others met with Xu Kan, Director of the Currency Department of the Ministry of Finance, the governing body, in Shanghai to present their opinions and request that efforts be made to remedy the situation when drafting the implementing regulations of the Banking Law. Director Xu stated that the Ministry of Finance had no authority to amend the Banking Law but promised to forward it to the Legislative Yuan for review. It is reported that Chen Guangfu and others may visit Director Xu again, still requesting that efforts be made to remedy the situation when drafting the implementing regulations of the Banking Law.

Municipal Chamber of Commerce Writes to the Tax Bureau Requesting that Tobacco Merchants be Allowed to Pay Taxes with Certificates 126

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce wrote to the Taxation Department of the Ministry of Finance yesterday: "To whom it may concern: On the 11th of this month, we received a letter from the local raw silk tobacco industry association stating that, according to members such as Jiang Wanchang and Jiang Dachang, since the implementation of the special tax, merchants have complied with the regulations and paid taxes, reporting and transporting goods for over a year, which has been convenient. However, recently, tobacco silk imported from Xiamen has been found to have blurred stamps on the boxes, or mismatched stamp numbers. The Jiangsu Stamp Tobacco and Alcohol Tax Bureau has ordered them to pay supplementary taxes, or even imposed fines. The merchants are in a hurry to sell the goods and are afraid of being fined, so they reluctantly paid the supplementary taxes. Tobacco silk is transported from Yongding, Fujian, to Shanghai, covering thousands of miles by land and water. The bamboo boxes are already damaged from being moved and bumped along the way, let alone the fragile paper stamps. The mismatched stamp numbers are because the tobacco silk is transported from Yongding to Zhangzhou, where it is then transferred to the merchants, who apply to the local tax bureau to pay the special tax. Since the number of goods received and transferred by the transferring merchants is large, and the number of merchants entrusting the transfer is also large, it is inevitable that there will be negligence when affixing the stamps. The local tax bureau, understanding the difficulties of the transferring merchants, does not scrutinize minor errors in the stamps when inspecting exports. Now, one party is considering the difficulties of the merchants and is lenient in allowing passage, while the other party is creating difficulties and imposing fines. Tax bureaus under the same national government have such contradictory practices, which go against the government's intention to facilitate merchants. Moreover, in fact, the tax certificate is the proof of tax payment, and the stamp is only to assist in verifying whether the tax has been paid. We request that the tax bureau not make unnecessary demands, consider the merchants' situation, and use the tax certificate as proof, not imposing fines based on the stamp. Furthermore, recently, the reporting and inspection of imported tobacco silk has taken a long time, affecting business, which is not insignificant. The association was instructed to submit a request to your association to alleviate the merchants' difficulties. After inquiring, it was found that when merchants transport tobacco to Shanghai, they pay the special tax in the local area according to regulations, obtain a tax certificate, and then affix the stamp to the surface of the goods. After inspection, the goods are allowed to be exported. The merchants have fulfilled their tax obligations, and the tax bureau has completed its audit responsibilities. When the goods arrive in Shanghai, checking whether there is a tax certificate accompanying the goods is sufficient to prevent smuggling. For goods that already have a tax certificate, it is unreasonable to demand supplementary taxes or impose fines on the grounds of blurred stamps or mismatched numbers. We believe that there is a need to improve the handling of this. Accordingly, we are writing to your office to request that you approve the above requests to alleviate the merchants' difficulties."

Association of Machine Factories Issues a Notice Soliciting Opinions from Various Factories on Insurance Issues 127

The Shanghai Association of Locally-Made Goods Machine Factories issued a notice yesterday soliciting opinions from various factories regarding factory insurance. The original text reads: "To whom it may concern: Factory insurance is intended to reduce burdens and protect against occasional dangers. However, insurance companies established by Chinese merchants often reinsure with foreign companies. The so-called 'adjusters' are completely biased and collude with insurance companies. Moreover, their regulations are mainly in English, which is contrary to Chinese commercial contracts. How can factory owners who have fire insurance obtain fair treatment? For example, the tragedy at Taiyi Factory occurred in August. The factory repeatedly contacted the insurance company, but the insurance company claimed that it had not received a report from the adjuster and has not yet indicated whether it will pay compensation, which is obviously unfair. The way to provide disaster relief is to be swift. The measures taken by these insurance companies are disappointing. Therefore, our association has resolved to organize an insurance committee to help plan, which is our duty. In order to gather information for reference, please provide the following information: 1. The name of the insurance company that provides fire insurance and the amount of the premium. 2. The circumstances of any past fires and whether compensation was paid. 3. Insurance experience and personal opinions on insurance law. Please provide your valuable advice on the above three points so that we can collect ideas and achieve the practical benefits of insurance. As this matter concerns the vital interests of the factory, we hereby request that you investigate and reply. We look forward to your reply."

Principles for Dividing Grain Reserves Pre-Determined by the Shanghai County Government 132

Shanghai City and County jointly own grain reserves and property. The conference of representatives from the city and county to change the area has been held repeatedly without any results. Now, the Municipal Government has ordered the reorganization of the Evaluation Committee to survey and divide the grain reserves. The County Government has designated five county committee members and sent a list to the Municipal Finance Bureau for review. The County Government's proposed pre-determined principles are recorded as follows: (Omitted above) The Shanghai Hospital should be reorganized under the City. The general situation has already been decided. However, the City's previous proposal was to estimate the price and sell the property, with the City and County dividing the funds, while the County proposed to divide the property. The City's latest instructions did not specify this point clearly. The statement that the Shanghai Hospital should also be assigned to the City is also very brief. In addition to the County appointing a representative to reply to the Municipal Finance Bureau and schedule a meeting, it is proposed to discuss the following principles: 1. The County still proposes to jointly survey the two properties, estimate the price, and divide the property and manage it according to the City and County's share. 2. Property plots should be pre-matched and evenly divided after valuation, with fertile and barren land balanced. If the value of an irregular plot cannot match the City's 63% and the County's 37% share, the County should request the right to preferentially designate the property to be accepted according to the estimated price, as a right to win the bid. 3. Since the Shanghai Hospital is to be retained by the City, it should be valued uniformly and included in the City's share. 4. Existing property and grain reserve property should be handled in the same way. After the division, if the County's property has already been occupied by the City, it should be transferred immediately. If it is needed in fact and cannot be transferred immediately, a lease agreement should be signed at market value.

Heavy Disaster in Haining, Additional Relief Funds Allocated 133

The Shanghai Chinese and Foreign Relief Society, the China Jisheng Society, the World Red Cross, the Bodhi Dharma Assembly, and other four charitable organizations, at the request of the Haining Drought Disaster Relief Association's Shanghai Office, designated specialists to go to Ning to jointly conduct emergency relief. County Magistrate Jiang Huiyue, who also served as the Director of Relief, personally accompanied them to the countryside to conduct investigations. Recently, the charitable organizations and the Haining Drought Relief Association's office have received reports from the directors of relief in various districts stating that the survey showed that nine out of ten homes were empty and the families had nothing. Moreover, since the autumn season, dysentery has been prevalent, and deaths have occurred in succession. New widows are everywhere. These diseases are not incurable, but the survivors of the disaster have no food, let alone medical care. Compared to the Yellow River flood, the scene is even more heartbreaking. All the medicines brought to Ning have been distributed, and due to the wide scope of the disaster and the shortage of funds, it is impossible to proceed without increasing the relief funds. The Chinese and Foreign Relief Society, etc., believing that the reports of the specialists on the ground are not exaggerated, have already allocated an additional 10,000 yuan to Ning. However, the Haining Drought Disaster Relief Association's Shanghai Office, because the funds for this emergency relief, in addition to the assistance of various charitable organizations and the surplus funds from the Renchen relief, have been advanced. The winter relief and spring relief are difficult to continue. Yesterday, they sent letters to fellow villagers in Shanghai and those who have raised funds in Tianjin, Beijing, Hangzhou, and other places, urging them to make efforts to raise funds. They will report the amount of funds raised in advance to plan for the overall situation.

Change of Guards of British Troops Stationed in Shanghai 134

According to the New Sound News Agency, the British troops stationed in Shanghai were originally the Second Battalion of the West Australia Regiment. Now that the time for the change of guards has arrived, the 27th Infantry Regiment arrived in Shanghai yesterday to take over the defense. According to the regiment, it arrived in Shanghai aboard the transport ship Dosterchia, with a total of 850 officers and soldiers. After arriving in port, they went to the British barracks on Nanjing Road to be stationed. The West Australia Regiment also boarded the Dosterchia and sailed to the Qinhuangdao area today.
