Free Talk

What We Need in Translations 214

— Miao Lie

Translation is indeed popular this year. First, [Literature] consecutively published two special issues on translation, followed by the emergence of [Translation] and [World Literature], and [Modern] also published a special issue on American literature to join in the fun. Translation, which has always been regarded as a matchmaker and not paid much attention to, actually has a chance to stand out, which is really a gratifying phenomenon.

However, what is slightly unsatisfactory is that most of the translated articles are short stories, and there is not a single one with a longer length. Moreover, some of these short stories are very familiar, as if I have seen them somewhere before. When I open old magazines to check, I can often find them. Of course, we are not against translating a work again and again, because we can often compare the merits of the translation from two different translations, but if we find too many, we can't help but feel that the waste of ability is a pity.

There are material reasons for the recent translation world's abundance of short stories and lack of long stories. We cannot complain about the translators. Because translators are also people, and they need material things to maintain their lives. In this year of sluggish publishing and lonely single-volume books, translating long translations is time-consuming, and it is not easy to find a way out after the translation is completed. As the saying goes, [Performing tricks with a stone mortar on your head is a lot of work and no reward]. In order to solve the material life, translators of course only have the one way of translating short stories.

However, in terms of the creative cultivation of young people, long translations are very necessary. Recently, there has been a problem in the literary world of why there are no great works produced, and observing the works of general young writers, most of them inevitably have the disadvantages of being superficial and empty. Often, they have very good themes and materials, but because they do not have the skills to describe them, they inevitably fail. If the works of foreign masters can be translated as much as possible, so that they can observe and learn from them, and understand how to layout and describe them in order to move people, I believe that in our barren literary circle, there will definitely be a few wonderful flowers.

So, what kind of translations do we need now?

Forgive me for saying boldly: we need a lot. Whether it is ancient or modern, as long as it is listed in the forest of world literature masterpieces and deserves it without shame and we have no translation, we need it.

Regarding the ancient ones, Homer's two epics, [Odyssey], already have a translation by Mr. Fu Donghua, but [Iliad] has not yet appeared, we need [Iliad]. In addition, the works of the three great Greek tragic writers, although most of them have been lost, there are still many that have been passed down to the world, and we all hope to have a chance to read them. Also, the Roman poet Virgil's [Aeneid], which was previously translated and published in part in Fiction Monthly, we also hope to have a complete translation.

Regarding the Renaissance era, Cervantes' [Don Quixote] complete translation, we really need it more urgently than any other work. Because among modern young people, terms such as Rudin type, Hamlet type, Bazarov type, and Don Quixote type are very popular. The first three have already been translated, but the latter only has a classical Chinese [Demon Hero Biography], which is not enough to satisfy our readers' hopes. Also, Shakespeare's six great tragedies, except for [Hamlet] [Macbeth] [Romeo and Juliet] which have been translated, others such as [Othello] [Julius Caesar] [Antony and Cleopatra] have not been translated, I hope someone can come forward to complete this work.

Although the works of the 17th and 18th centuries are no longer to our taste, there are several famous works, such as Milton's [Paradise Regained], Bunyan's [The Pilgrim's Progress], Richardson's [Pamela], Fielding's [Tom Jones], Goldsmith's [The Vicar of Wakefield], etc., and we also hope that someone can translate them for us to read.

There are many famous works in the 19th century, and most of these famous works do not have Chinese translations. If we want to list them all, it is definitely not something that can be accommodated in a short space. Here, we can only say some roughly. In England, we need Scott's [Waverley Novels], Dickens' [A Tale of Two Cities], Hardy's [Jude the Obscure], Byron's [Don Juan], etc. In France, we need Balzac's [La Comedie Humaine], Zola's [Les Rougon-Macquart], etc. In Russia, we need Goncharov's [Oblomov], Dostoevsky's [The Brothers Karamazov], etc. In Germany, we need Goethe's [Faust] Second Alley, Hauptmann's [Einsame Menschen], etc. In the United States, we need Irving's [The Spy], Hawthorne's [The Scarlet Letter], [The Shallows], the Italian D'Annunzio's [Fire], etc., which are also what we urgently need to read.

As for modern masterpieces, such as Shaw's dramas, Gorky Sinclair, and the novels of the New Russian writers, although many have been introduced, long works such as Romain Rolland's [Jean-Christophe], Galsworthy's [Forsyte], etc., still need the continued efforts of translators.

I am not a celebrity, and I don't have the courage to open a reading list on behalf of young people. The ones listed here are just what I personally feel are more needed, although they may represent the opinions of some people.

Passing Through Linggi Lama (Part 1) 215

— Fei Er

After emerging from the edge of Shangda city, the car sped along the forest lane. Because there were almost no pedestrians on the road except in the residential areas of villages, cities, and botanical gardens, the two drivers were eager to return to their homes, so the car was driven at the highest possible speed. Along the way, only a white sky and dark green tree shadows flashed by, and occasionally a few colorful cars passed by.

After boarding at Wan Tao Durian, the car continued to travel at yesterday's speed, and the scenery seen was not much different. Once one is accustomed to traveling through the lush lanes of the equator, one will have the illusion that except for the car one is in rushing madly, the world is completely still.

However, as the car approached Linggi Lama, the situation was a little different. The car had just passed through an American magnate's rubber plantation, and the rows of workers' residences, lying flat like pigeon coops, had just passed. The image of the Javanese workers' [sarongs] drying outside the doors, fluttering in the wind like the shadows of flags on ships, had not yet been forgotten, when the car climbed a small hill. Because the rubber trees had not been planted for long, when the car reached the top of this hill, looking out over the low bushes below, one could see a scene never before seen in the equatorial zone. Before one's eyes were low bushes stretching to the horizon, the red sun was scorching in the sky, and the village clusters were undulating, making one feel as if one were in a vast desert. The highway lay winding through this red land, like the footprints left by travelers and camel caravans in the desert.

As the car passed through this small market town with only a few small shops, Chinese shopkeepers and Javanese workers glanced at the car, and it lightly kissed them. A sign written in black Chinese characters on white cloth, "[XX Orchard Chinese School]," was displayed in front of a small wooden house. This made me extremely happy, as I am well aware of the difficulties in establishing overseas Chinese children's schools among workers and small merchants; and in such a small place, such a simple overseas Chinese elementary school was showing, which was truly heartening.

The car drove out of the vast plantation (which took more than an hour, and it is said that the dismissal of workers in this plantation later caused a small disturbance, because the workers were extremely numerous and most of them were dismissed). Soon, it arrived at Linggi Lama.

Random Thoughts on Self-Cooking 217

— Wei Zhongtian

– Snippets of Life Studying in Japan –

First of all, I must first introduce our group. There are four people in our group, three of whom are a bit wild, and only one is a bit more serious. That's why we all call her "Big Sister". In fact, she is much older than us. The first person in our group is R.Y., the second is Mambo, who used to have mixed up some days in the army.

Sometimes, she is even wilder than B.Y. The third is "Big Sister", and the fourth is me. Because they are all women, and I am the only exception, our group is under female rule.

Now, let's talk about our motivation for cooking ourselves. Because we live in the same boarding house and go to the same school, everyone feels that the food in the restaurants is not good and costs a lot of money. Cooking ourselves is more economical and delicious, so everyone started paying attention to cooking themselves.

One morning a week ago, we held a food meeting and passed the following resolutions: 1. Each person contributes nine yuan per month for expenses, which can be increased as needed. 2. The four people are divided into two groups, and each day one group is responsible for buying vegetables, washing rice, cooking, washing dishes and chopsticks, etc. 3. Lunch is at 11:00 am, and dinner is at 6:00 pm. 4. You cannot only buy the dishes you like to eat. These resolutions were implemented from the day we started cooking.

Now, we have been living a self-cooking life for a week. Every day we work happily and eat happily. Our friends envy our life and envy the dishes we cook, so friends often come to eat. Mambo's cooking tastes very good, she is really an expert, but she is too bad, she brags, she says she used to cook for nine months in Changsha, she can cook very good dishes, but the fact tells us that the dishes she cooks are the worst, often cooking the beef like a piece of cloth, I laugh at her, I say: "You can only write novels, you are a beginner at cooking, you should do a three-year apprenticeship." But she denies it, she either says the fire is too big today, or she says she forgot to put soy sauce today.

Yesterday evening it was Mambo's turn to cook again, and Wang Ying happened to come to our place. We asked her to stay for dinner, and she said: "Okay!" So we bought some more vegetables and some noodles. The dishes last night were really well cooked, which everyone agreed on. During the meal, Wang Ying said: "I eat that Japanese food that doesn't suit my taste every day, it's so bitter, I feel like I'm in a foreign country every day. After eating this dish tonight, I feel like I'm back in China."

We also discussed that we should have a big meal during the New Year. Wang Ying suggested buying a lot of wine. I suggested buying at least two chickens, and proposed to kill a pig, which made us laugh so hard our stomachs hurt. Each of us is not very young, and we have also done a little work in society, and we have learned a set of "sophisticated" faces, however, when we are with friends, we all show a pure childlike heart, just like children.

I believe we will gain weight living like this, and it is also a student life without any responsibility.

Wandering Minstrel (7) 218

— Lu Fen

With moist light flashing in his eyes, he suddenly stood up, unusually angry, patted his temples and yelled:

"Fish can still be eaten when they grow up, but people! People, they can only rot."

He ignored the net casters and the pedestrians on the bridge who were laughing at him mockingly, tears glistening on his withered cheeks. His name was also extended from "fragrant grass" to "liar," "conscience"... As for whether "liar" was condemning "fragrant grass" himself, or others, people never cared about this aspect.

He returned to the inn with the weariness of old age, and it became lively. The waiter flitted back and forth, like a puppy welcoming its master; affectionately twisting his arm. He dodged back and forth, now with an impatient expression, definitely not angry. The waiter understood, there was nothing to do now - he neither watched operas at night, nor gambled, he only drank alcohol before going to bed.

Regarding drinking, the waiter put it well:

"If you don't gamble, don't drink, what does a person do? At most, it's just a hundred years, lying under the coffin boards in all four seasons, enduring and enduring, a good death is like blowing away ashes!" But looking at "Fragrant Grass'" gradually purpling face, he would immediately switch his tone, saying sadly: "Old friend, you should turn back! In youth, life is like a thread in the sky. You fear nothing on earth. But when you're old, you should take some precautions."

The waiter remembered these words clearly. He had been a bartender in this inn for more than ten years, and had never said them to a single passerby. Only "Fragrant Grass" was the exception.

"Fragrant Grass" also understood the weight of these words between people, but he could not take the sincere advice as a lullaby. Once, the waiter had a falling out with him and didn't bring him wine. For an entire night, he seemed to be seriously ill, moaning like an opium addict in pain, tears streaming down. In fact, that suffering was beyond imagination. A person, just a single person, after endless humiliations from birth. These humiliations accumulate over the days and months until the age of fifty or sixty, and they have an unbearable weight. Turn back. The terrifying past is like crisscrossing harbors, like a sea of churning black waves. How can he cross that boundless night covered in black fur? Except by drinking wine. Otherwise, it's better to die.

"Without drinking wine, the sins are deeper than the sea!"

There is such a famous saying. If the depth of sins is measured by the amount of suffering endured, these words are correct. He believed it to be the truth.

He lowered his head and tapped the table with his chopsticks, making an unpleasant, greasy sound. This was a ditty that could be heard everywhere on the quietly blue-green Huai River, a melody mixed with joy and sorrow. At first, it was very rhythmic, but as time went on, it was just like those ditties themselves, all mixed up.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Essays

On "Boasting" and "Mutual Disdain" 219

— Dan Ran

Modern literati have accepted the legacy of previous generations of literati, but they have also accepted many of the characteristics of previous generations of literati at the same time.

Previous generations of literati had many characteristics, and among the most commonly existing characteristics among previous generations of literati, and which have been further evolved after being accepted by modern literati, is probably "boasting" and "mutual disdain."

Why do literati boast and disdain each other? We can summarize several reasons from articles of the argumentative type: the reason for "boasting" is due to "moral character and literary talent, both admired," "the like-mindedness of worthy people;" the reason for "mutual disdain" is due to "lack of knowledge and skill," "unwillingness to associate with the depraved." In fact, these are all superficial words, and at heart it is not necessarily the case. Ultimately, it is nothing more than the worship of "self," the superior ones inevitably "blindly feel the elephant," stubbornly adhering to their own opinions; the inferior ones are completely enthusiastic about the pursuit of "fame."

Originally, very few literati in ancient China married books to real life. It is difficult to find the position of books of the type of "governance and statecraft writings" in the Complete Library of the Four Treasuries, so literati have become some bookworms full of square-hat air. As long as they privately study a few ancient people or a few classics, they "carve a mark on a boat to find a sword," stubbornly guarding a corner. If you feel an elephant's leg, you will speak eloquently; if I feel an elephant's trunk, I will go against you with flags and drums. Due to the arrogance of the square-hat air, they will pull together their own kind and "boast" to make a big scene. "Abusive words are never good," and "mutual disdain" is inevitable. This is still the superior ones.

The most intolerable and most common characteristic of literati is the enthusiasm for the pursuit of "fame."

Originally, "fame and fortune" have been the symbols of life in China since ancient times. Perhaps because the word "fortune" is too vulgar, ancient literati have been particularly enthusiastic about "fame." Like the so-called "climbing the dragon" nowadays, the first thing is always to obtain "fame." Only after having "fame" can it be used as a stepping stone for all attempts, so "fame" has become the first meaning for literati.

Because "self's" "fame" is the goal, in addition to showing "goods," they have to use some means. "Boasting" and "mutual disdain" are the "only way." "Boasting" can form a fortress by itself, joining hands to "climb the dragon," which is considered successful, the essence of the "mutual aid doctrine." "Mutual disdain" is like "enemies meeting, especially red-eyed," a melee of thirty rounds is necessary to see who is superior. This may be Darwin's "theory of evolution."

Therefore, "literati have no morals" has become a common evaluation by the general public.

The highest and most supreme magic weapon is still to nakedly present the "goods" to the audience. "Bystanders see clearly," and the audience will not fail to distinguish between black and white. "Boasting" and "mutual disdain" do not seem to be the right paths.

Flower Girl 220

— TT

The flower girl, Cui'er, every early morning, her calling out to sell flowers always缠绕 around in front of my apartment.

The sound is sharp and thin, clear and slightly sad. Whenever such a sad sound struck my eardrum, my heart would sometimes feel a slight pang of sadness. I went near the window, opened the window, looked down, and asked her:

"Cui'er, is business good?"

"Not too bad, sir." She always answered this way, and then immediately called out to sell again. She dared not relax her business for a moment, hoping that a basket of fresh flowers would turn into one copper coin after another, following her voice.

She called out from door to door. If her voice rang in front of someone's door, and the front door or back door suddenly opened inward, then her silver-colored thin face would, without a doubt, immediately flash a smile. Rushing forward, then a string of words like "Madam, Sir, Miss" would constantly burst out of her mouth, her attitude so sincere, so pitiful.

She was often like this, never stopping even on rainy days. Therefore, the people near my apartment gradually became familiar with her, especially me. I was confident that I knew her better than others. This was not because I had traded with her more often, but because I admired and sympathized with her diligence in her own business, so I often talked to her, sometimes buying one or two flowers from her, naturally never haggling over the price. She also seemed to think of me as someone

Page 20

She could confide her inner thoughts to.

In this way, I learned that she had only one mother. Her father had died when she was two or three years old. Her mother had worked hard to raise her, but now she couldn't. She couldn't rely on her mother anymore. Her mother's health had been ruined by overwork, and illness refused to leave her for even a step.

One morning, I was sound asleep when suddenly, a "tuk tuk tuk" sound woke me up. I perked up my ears and listened quietly. I immediately realized that someone was knocking on the door. It turned out to be Cui'er standing at the door, shedding tears. She cried out, "Sir," and then sobbed.

"What's the matter?" I asked in surprise.

Only then did she stop crying and slowly say:

"Sir, please do me a favor and give me a few cents."

"Okay, but why are you crying?"

"Mom doesn't look too good." She couldn't help crying again.

I took the few cents I had on me and gave them to her. She took them and quickly walked downstairs.

After that, I didn't hear her calling out to sell flowers anymore. I didn't even dare to guess the reason for this.

They Brought Hunger Back Again 221

— Xin Bo

By the Bund 222

— Xi Bai

Shanghai, you are mocking people, you are bewildering people!

Red, green, white... all the bright lights are as bright as a beauty's eyes, bewitching so many young people!

Noises, clamoring sounds. How confusing and disturbing is the peace of human nerves!

Solemn and tall buildings compete with the pyramids! This reminds people of the greatness and immortality of the pyramids and the everlasting Great Wall in the long-dead slave era! The glorious lights of the Roman palaces illuminate Western culture that will never be extinguished.

But oh, the glittering lights on the spire of your building are the heroic fairy spirit of the wage-earning slaves!

Oh, who says this place is dark? Doesn't it have the jewels you decorated it with, emitting bright light?

Oh, who says this place is ugly? Isn't your face already covered with dazzling colored powder, smeared with lipstick, and your body covered with beautiful gauze clothes?

Ah, beauty! You will use all your skills to groom all your ugliness.

My wisdom grows here, this is my third hometown.

I once saw off guests at the Huangpu River, shedding tears of farewell for those guests!

Ah, when we parted in the old days, it was also such a bleak scene with fallen leaves floating in the heart of the river.

But now, the Huangpu River is still there, and the river water flows in vain. Where have the guests gone now? Ah, could you know his news?

Empty sadness, remembering the short and the long, the fallen leaves are still the same.

However, oh, my heart today is no longer as fragile as it used to be.

I remember what the guest once said: Please look at the flowing waves in the heart of the river: wave after wave after wave, and the boat surges in the heart of the wave: although the boat has suffered twists and turns, the boat remains intact. As long as you move forward, there will be no danger! Otherwise, if you don't move forward or backward, only the surrounding boats will smash you to pieces!

Ah! Now I see that a boat in the heart of the river is still there!

Beside the Sickbed 223

— Cui Ying

It's been a long time since I've been sick, a rare miracle for me. For seven or eight years, according to the doctor, I have lung disease. Getting this disease is quite comfortable. At that time, I was still in school, and I was "an official" not going to school. Hearing the classmates say that they had been up for several nights during the big exams, I hoped that this disease would last forever. Sure enough, for seven or eight years now, every doctor with a stethoscope has proven that I have lung disease, and I have been comfortable like this until now; not staying up late, not running into trouble in society. But if you think I inherited a considerable inheritance, you are wrong. Writing a little prose like "Beside the Sickbed" in a comfortable illness can prove it.

I started knowing I had this disease naturally after coughing up blood. Most Chinese people get this disease this way. The reason is not that Chinese people pay too little attention to hygiene, it's just that too few are blessed with the fortune to spend a few dollars to go to the doctor to check their health.

Coughing up blood is really a big deal. In fact, although it is "comfortable," I am somewhat afraid of dying in my heart. Going to the doctor for treatment is even more terrible. He said it was third-stage lung disease. He himself diligently smoked a cigar, and disinfected all the instruments with alcohol desperately, as if I was already "gone."

Returning home, I read some lung disease self-treatment ABCs on the sickbed, and ate milk, eggs, and cod liver oil for every meal. At the same time, a friend studying at the medical school came to give me calcium injections every day for free. Worry-free, I sent the first day of the year to the thirtieth day. When I was happy to sleep, I slept for a lifetime. If I wanted to get up and walk around, no one would stop me. For seven or eight years, there has been no sign of death. But it's also strange, my self-treatment can be said to be perfect; staying in a sanatorium at most to shine a sun lamp, I also sunbathe for half an hour every day. This year, encouraged by a friend (the one who gave the injections for free), I spent a few yuan and a few cents to go to the doctor's door. After listening with a stethoscope, he meticulously tapped on my ribs with his orchid fingers. Humph, the sound was a "dong dong" sound. The lung disease self-treatment ABC told me that it was called a clear sound, which is a good phenomenon in the lungs. However, the doctor still shook his head, which made me suspect that the doctor's shaking his head had some connection with his business; he insisted that I take an X-ray, saying it was a terrible third stage and that I had to be hospitalized. This was in early spring this year. After passing the winter, I lived another year, and I still read my self-treatment ABC.

That being said, isn't this disease comfortable enough? I don't know how many stages lung disease is divided into. One stage can last for seven or eight years. If there are ten stages, it cannot be said that it is not long-lived. In this case, cholera vomiting and diarrhea, killing several lives in an hour, is terrifying!

School-Age Children 224

— Bai Li

Novel

Liu Desheng in Jiangxi (7) 225

— Wan Guoan

(4) The Stage Could Have Been in Revolt

The big, dark fellow pondered, "I've lived this long and never stood before so many people to speak. Today, they've hoisted me up like a hawk! Damn it! I'll just say a few words, no matter how bad it is!" The guy was even more energetic, standing straight as a military telephone pole at the edge of the stage, his mouth open for a long time, but no sound came out. He was really getting anxious! The small guy standing behind him, seeing things weren't right, quickly leaned over and whispered:

[Didn't a female comrade teach you last night? Just say what she taught you!]

The big, dark fellow became even more flustered. Last night he was only focused on enjoying the moment, and didn't hear what she said. Today was going to be a total disaster!

[The White Army is not as good as the Red Army! Say it!] The small guy was acting as a prompter.

[Right! The White Army is not as good as the Red Army, our National Revolutionary Army is better.] The big, dark fellow felt quite pleased with himself for saying this, but the stage could have been in revolt.

[Counter-revolutionary – Down with him!

Down with this counter-revolutionary!]

At first, the big, dark fellow thought the audience was cheering him on. But then he looked closely and saw that things were not right! Those skinny devils all had their mouths wide open, as if they wanted to devour him alive! The big, dark fellow wanted to turn around and run, but the guy acting as the prompter grabbed him, and shouted at the same time –

[Comrades: Don't make a fuss! He hasn't made himself clear, let him speak again!]

[You say the Red Army is good, the National Revolutionary Army is murderous arsonists!]

The big, dark fellow was terrified. He couldn't escape, and he had to learn to speak:

[The Red Army is good, the National Revolutionary Army fights well!]

[At that moment, the big, dark fellow rolled off the stage, landing face-first in the dirt. If the slogan [soldiers don't fight soldiers] hadn't been in effect, the big, dark fellow would have been skinned alive, at the very least.]

A few days later, the big, dark fellow had a red cloth strip tied around his neck. The big, dark fellow didn't bother to study the color of the strip. That morning, when he tied the strip, he muttered to himself – "Whether it's stained with pus, blood, or dog blood, it's all the same."

Shen Bao Local Supplement Film Special

The Success Story of Adventure Film Director Van Dyke 230

— Donglin

Van Dyke, a famous Hollywood adventure film director, is the director of the film [Eskimo], which was once shown in Shanghai.

Van Dyke's father was a lawyer, but he died nine days after his birth. At that time, his mother, who was only twenty-one years old, had to join a traveling troupe to perform everywhere for a living. When they traveled to Chartres, Van Dyke was taken by his grandfather to be raised in his home. It was here that Van Dyke was able to complete his secondary education.

After graduating from middle school, he went out into society alone to seek self-reliance. He had worked as a handyman in a station, a salesman in a lighting store, and a groom in a freight store. Later, he joined his mother's traveling troupe.

However, he soon left. Afterwards, he engaged in work in coal mines, ranches, and logging.

In 1915, when he was twenty-seven years old, he was spotted by the famous director Griffith in Greensike, which was the starting point of his new life. Director Griffith loved his ability to work continuously for eighteen hours. When he started filming the masterpiece [Intolerance], he promoted him to assistant director. From that time on, he was determined to serve the film industry for life.

In 1928, for the sake of the exterior scenes of O'Brien's [White Shadows in the South Seas], he and Director Flaherty crossed over to Tahiti Island together. Unfortunately, Director Flaherty suddenly fell ill, and the filming of the exterior scenes had to be suspended for a while. However, Van Dyke took over for Director Flaherty, and about seven months later, he finished filming everything and returned to Hollywood. After the film was released, it won great praise, and Van Dyke suddenly became a famous director in Hollywood.

After gaining fame from his debut work, he was dispatched to Tahiti Island to shoot exterior scenes for a romantic love film starring Ramon Novarro. He finished shooting it in just six weeks, and the film also received praise from all sides. As a result, he greatly developed his skills in producing adventure films, and the famous [Eskimo] was released to the public.

Most film directors, under the supervision of managers, etc. in the studio, can shoot very good films, but once they leave and go to desolate islands or snow-covered mountains, their qualifications as directors are bound to be equal to zero. But Van Dyke is an exception. Even if he goes to the wilderness of Africa to shoot exterior scenes, he can still exert his directorial talents without regret.

Film Reviews

Review of [One Night of Love] 231

— Shuofu

One Night of Love

Da Guangming Cinema Screening

The sound of jazz music is as popular and crazy as can be in the city. Radio broadcasts, records, and even idlers walking on the street will always hum a few new movie songs.

From a long time until now, these vulgar tunes of [irregular Zheng sounds] have really made people tired of listening to them. Surprisingly, in this [One Night of Love], my ears were washed, and my appetite was opened. Undoubtedly, this is a successful work of classical light opera.

Speaking of opera, of course, it is not comparable to turning vulgar tunes such as [folk songs] and [mountain songs] into something that is neither fish nor fowl. This is [pouring out blood from the heart], [fine-tuning the musical scales], carefully considering the six laws and five tones, and undergoing several refinements and arrangements before it can be released to the public. A musician's fame depends entirely on the performance of the opera he directs one night. This is such a bright and great thing in art!

Early on, I was fascinated by music, and I was immediately devoted to a kind of [popular song]. Later, I gradually became able to listen to opera. After I had a considerable understanding of Western opera, I felt that popular songs were really shallow and inferior, and even made my ears crawl.

The plot of [One Night of Love] is very suitable for opera performance. Naturally, harmoniously, symmetrically, and beautifully, it writes out artistic life effortlessly and humorously. It is not only the success of Director Victor Schertainder, but also due to the richness of the plot.

The female lead, Grace Moore, sings with a very high quality. As for using clichés such as [clear voice], [piercing clouds and cracking rocks], [surrounding the beams three times] to praise her, I think it is looking down on her. Only the so-called [glorious voice] that is praised by the general public in Hollywood can be considered accurate.

Supporting actors such as Camina Di (Italian) as the singing teacher, Albani (Spanish) as the pianist, and Mona Bellini as another singer, all complement the brilliance of this play. Only Toul Bowl's Billy has failed to fully display his talents.

In the play, the two operas [Carmen] and [Madame Butterfly] are originally very different foreign styles of songs. When sung by Ms. Grace, they can be compared to Lucrezia Bori, which is also the reason why she is so popular among the new singers in Hollywood.

This film can be considered a fine work among the recent musical films. After watching it, I heard the so-called creative singing of China in the recent radio broadcasts. Recalling that recently, Hollywood business travelers, when they came to China, thought that tunes like Peach Blossom River could represent the recent Chinese national character, I simply got goosebumps all over my body.

Struggling with the pain of illness to write this introductory review, although it is a suffering, it is also quite pleasant. Perhaps good artistic works have the effect of sending away poverty and driving away malaria.

Review of [The Sea Killers] 232

— You Jing

“The Sea Killers” - Golden Field

As the title indicates, this film should be a strange underwater adventure. But in reality, there are so many descriptions of the sea surface; and the exploration process, which should be the climax of this film, is not very dangerous.

Here, let's offer some opinions as a documentary about the sea.

As a long subtitle in front of the screen, it says: In 1868, a ship carrying gold set sail from San Francisco and was sunk by pirates in the waters of Mexico. It has never been salvaged.

The picture starts with the voyage of a team of adventurers seeking to find the remaining gold, followed by many records of fishing, otter catching, whale swimming, and seagull flying seen during the voyage. Finally, they reach the Crystal Rock where the sunken ship is located, and a person takes a [lifeline] to sink to the bottom of the sea, encountering a shark, which breaks his [lifeline]. His companions return in disappointment and sorrow.

Since, as mentioned earlier, there are not many dangerous scenes or tense atmosphere, the impression given to the audience from beginning to end is not deep. In some places, it is clear that the fishermen used sharp forks to throw into the sea, but when the fish that was caught was pulled onto the boat, what was taken out of the fish's mouth was a hook. This gives people a feeling of unreality. Also, such as several times when the caught fish is pulled up from the sea, in addition to the fish's struggle, due to the different size and nature of the fishermen themselves, they are mostly pulled onto the boat in the same way, which makes the original so-called [strange] a bit commonplace.

Only the sea otter escaping, the seaweed swirling, and the group of fish vying for a shellfish after the underwater explorer cut it open gave us extremely beautiful impressions and wild fun. When the caught Corvina is lifted up: a tall person is used to compare it, and it is not even as long as the fish. It is quite commendable to pull open the fish's mouth to show the length of the mouth and the sharpness of the teeth.

The description says that someone on the ship unintentionally killed a dolphin that seafarers regarded as a close friend. Therefore, the whole ship was shocked, but we did not see this scene on the screen. The blue shark, which is the protagonist of this sea exploration, and is called the devil who kills people on the sea without blinking an eye, is only shown to us without showing its ferocity.

[Confused Happiness] - Nanjing Screens Joe E. Brown's Hilarious and Exciting Masterpiece, the Wide-Mouthed Star with a Born Clown Face

Gong Jianong in [Homeless] 233

— Fire

In Li Pingqian's [Homeless], the lives and struggles of people in today's society are depicted calmly and profoundly. The play describes a hardworking dock worker, although his daily wages are so meager that he cannot support a family of three, he can never forget to drink old wine and gamble on Pai Gow. As a result, he lost his only four cents. He thought that his wife and children were waiting for him hungry, waiting for his four cents to buy medicine to treat his son who was unfortunately burned by fire. Thinking and thinking, the fire of anger disturbed his painful nerves, so he accidentally beat someone to death and was sentenced to twenty years of imprisonment. After coming out of prison, he was already an old man with gray hair. (But)

Film Novel

相逢恨晚（The Age of Innocence）（四） 234

— Li Xin

A few days passed, and May felt something was strange, so she went to ask Newland: "Newland, you've been here for a few days, and you hardly speak, as if you're unhappy. What's wrong? Newland, tell me, is there someone else? Tell me honestly. I've felt it strange for a long time—ever since we got engaged." Her eyes fixed on him, her lips trembling slightly. After a moment, she said again: "Newland, tell me, could a person easily do something wrong?" Newland remained silent for a long time, and May then said: "Newland, if you feel you've done something wrong, if you have another beloved, I don't want you to be separated from her because of me...no matter what..." She tried hard to be brave, but she couldn't hold on. Suddenly, she started to cry, reaching out her hands to embrace him, clinging to him like a frightened child. Newland remembered his purpose in coming to Florida, and he couldn't help but scold himself for being too cruel. He hugged her tightly, wiped away her tears, and comforted her, saying: "Oh, May, I don't have anyone else, but I want to marry you immediately. Long engagements are okay for some people, but I..." May raised her head and said softly to him: "I always thought I loved you, but I never knew how deeply I loved you until today. Oh, Newland, do you love me too? Do you? Can't you live without me? Is that right?" Newland was a tender-hearted person by nature, and at this moment, he felt compelled to tell a lie. So he deceived her, saying: "That's right. I can't live without you." As he spoke, he kissed her. That evening, he left Florida and returned to New York.

After Newland returned to New York, he was afraid that seeing Elaine would make him forget the impressions he had gained in Florida, so he didn't go to see Elaine for a week. But after a week, he couldn't stand it anymore. So one afternoon, he ran to Mrs. Minggu's house for tea, hoping to run into Elaine there. That day, he found Elaine in the flower room, she was cutting roses. He couldn't help but call out: "Elaine!" Elaine saw him and immediately put down the roses and scissors, stood silently for a moment, then turned around, reached out her hand to Newland, and cried out: "My darling, my treasure!" Newland hugged her, and the two of them couldn't speak for a long time. Later, she pushed him away, reached out her hand, and touched a blade of grass's tender flower. The flower closed immediately at her touch and withered very quickly. Elaine then said softly: "Newland, didn't you see that little flower just now? Life touched it, and it died. Newland, we have also been touched by life, and we will also die." Newland mumbled: "Elaine, Elaine. Don't say those words! We've only just begun to live! When I was in Florida, I must have become neurotic. I'll go tell May now! She'll understand. I'll go to Florida again to see May in the next few days. We can't be separated! We'll never have to be afraid again." Elaine listened, leaned against the door of the flower room, and muttered to herself: "Oh, God! Why did I come back?" Newland hugged her again and said: "For this. For this." He kissed her. Suddenly, someone outside shouted: "Newland, Newland! Where are you?" Newland's hands dropped down. He and Elaine looked at each other, because it was May Welland's voice, May rushed towards the flower room, like a child who hadn't seen her mother for half a day. (To be continued)
